<p><b>Jamie Richard Vardy</b> (<i><a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Né">né</a></i> <b>Gill</b>; born 11 January 1987) is an English professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Striker_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Striker (association football)">striker</a> for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a>. Vardy has also played for the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national team</a>.
</p><p>After being released by <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a> at the age of 16, Vardy began his senior career with <a href="/wiki/Stocksbridge_Park_Steels_F.C." title="Stocksbridge Park Steels F.C.">Stocksbridge Park Steels</a>, breaking into the first team in 2007 and spending three seasons there before joining <a href="/wiki/Northern_Premier_League" title="Northern Premier League">Northern Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/FC_Halifax_Town" title="FC Halifax Town">FC Halifax Town</a> in 2010. Scoring 25 goals in his debut season, he won the club's "Player's Player of the Year" award and then moved to <a href="/wiki/Conference_Premier" class="mw-redirect" title="Conference Premier">Conference Premier</a> club <a href="/wiki/Fleetwood_Town_F.C." title="Fleetwood Town F.C.">Fleetwood Town</a> in August 2011 for an undisclosed fee. He scored 31 league goals in his first season at his new team, winning the team's "Player of the Year" award as they won the division.
</p><p>In May 2012, Vardy signed for Leicester City in the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Non-League_football" title="Non-League football">non-League</a> record transfer fee of £1&#160;million and helped the team win the Championship in 2014. In the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Premier_League" title="2015–16 Premier League">2015–16 Premier League</a> season, he scored in eleven consecutive Premier League matches, breaking <a href="/wiki/Ruud_van_Nistelrooy" title="Ruud van Nistelrooy">Ruud van Nistelrooy</a>'s record, and was voted the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Season" title="Premier League Player of the Season">Premier League Player of the Season</a> and <a href="/wiki/FWA_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="FWA Footballer of the Year">FWA Footballer of the Year</a> as outsiders Leicester won the title. He won the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Premier League Golden Boot</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Premier_League" title="2019–20 Premier League">2019–20 season</a>, becoming the oldest player to win the award.<sup id="cite_ref-GB_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
He also sits in 2nd place for most goals scored against top 6 clubs, with 38.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Vardy made his international debut in June 2015 and was selected for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Vardy was born in <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, South Yorkshire,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and grew up in the Hillsborough area of inner-city Sheffield. His father was a crane worker and his mother worked at a solicitors.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steels07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Steels07.jpg/220px-Steels07.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Steels07.jpg/330px-Steels07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2f/Steels07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="432" data-file-height="279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steels07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vardy with <a href="/wiki/Stocksbridge_Park_Steels_F.C." title="Stocksbridge Park Steels F.C.">Stocksbridge Park Steels</a> in 2007 (back row, third from right)</div></div></div>
<p>Vardy was in the youth system at <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a> but was released at age 16.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He then played at <a href="/wiki/Stocksbridge_Park_Steels_F.C." title="Stocksbridge Park Steels F.C.">Stocksbridge Park Steels</a>, where he made his way through the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_team" title="Reserve team">reserve team</a> and into the first team making his debut under <a href="/wiki/Manager_(association_football)" title="Manager (association football)">manager</a> Gary Marrow in 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-Departure_of_Vardy_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Departure_of_Vardy-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> earning £30 a week at the club.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> After impressive displays, a number of <a href="/wiki/English_Football_League" title="English Football League">Football League</a> teams became interested and in 2009 he spent a week on trial with <a href="/wiki/Crewe_Alexandra_F.C." title="Crewe Alexandra F.C.">Crewe Alexandra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vardy_is_on_trial_at_Crewe_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vardy_is_on_trial_at_Crewe-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> A move did not materialise and he later turned down a short-term contract with <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Halifax_beat_League_clubs_to_land_Vardy_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halifax_beat_League_clubs_to_land_Vardy-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2010, manager <a href="/wiki/Neil_Aspin" title="Neil Aspin">Neil Aspin</a>, a long time admirer of Vardy's talents, signed him for <a href="/wiki/FC_Halifax_Town" title="FC Halifax Town">FC Halifax Town</a> for a fee of £15,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Halifax_Town:_Aspin&#39;s_excited_about_Vardy_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halifax_Town:_Aspin&#39;s_excited_about_Vardy-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He made his debut on 21 August 2010 in the home match against <a href="/wiki/Buxton_F.C." title="Buxton F.C.">Buxton</a>, scoring the winning goal in a match that ended 2–1 to his new club.<sup id="cite_ref-Match_Update_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Match_Update-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Vardy had a successful first season with "the Shaymen" finishing as the club's top goalscorer with 25 goals from 37 appearances<sup id="cite_ref-Halifax1011_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halifax1011-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and being voted the Player's Player of the Season. Towards the end of the season he came close to scoring a <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> of hat-tricks but failed to find a third goal in Halifax's 3–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Nantwich_Town_F.C." title="Nantwich Town F.C.">Nantwich Town</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Match_Report_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Match_Report-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> His goals helped secure the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Premier_League" title="Northern Premier League">Northern Premier League</a> Premier Division title for the 2010–11 season.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Season_In_Stats_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Season_In_Stats-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Vardy started the 2011–12 season with Halifax and scored three goals in the opening four matches of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-Soccerway_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soccerway-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleetwood_Town">Fleetwood Town</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Fleetwood Town">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:92px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamie_Vardy_07-04-12.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Jamie_Vardy_07-04-12.png/90px-Jamie_Vardy_07-04-12.png" decoding="async" width="90" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Jamie_Vardy_07-04-12.png/135px-Jamie_Vardy_07-04-12.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Jamie_Vardy_07-04-12.png/180px-Jamie_Vardy_07-04-12.png 2x" data-file-width="603" data-file-height="2032" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamie_Vardy_07-04-12.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vardy playing for <a href="/wiki/Fleetwood_Town_F.C." title="Fleetwood Town F.C.">Fleetwood Town</a> in 2012</div></div></div>
<p>After just over a year with Halifax, Vardy signed for <a href="/wiki/Conference_Premier" class="mw-redirect" title="Conference Premier">Conference Premier</a> club <a href="/wiki/Fleetwood_Town_F.C." title="Fleetwood Town F.C.">Fleetwood Town</a> for an undisclosed fee.<sup id="cite_ref-Vardy_Joins_Fleetwood_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vardy_Joins_Fleetwood-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He made his debut the same day in a 0–0 home draw with <a href="/wiki/York_City_F.C." title="York City F.C.">York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fleetwood_Town_0-0_York_City_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fleetwood_Town_0-0_York_City-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goals for the club in his third appearance, scoring twice in a 3–2 win away to <a href="/wiki/Kettering_Town_F.C." title="Kettering Town F.C.">Kettering Town</a> on 3 September. The following week he scored another two goals against <a href="/wiki/Gateshead_F.C." title="Gateshead F.C.">Gateshead</a> at <a href="/wiki/Highbury_Stadium_(Fleetwood)" title="Highbury Stadium (Fleetwood)">Highbury Stadium</a>, including one in added time. He scored twice for a third consecutive match when on in the 3–1 away win against <a href="/wiki/Ebbsfleet_United_F.C." title="Ebbsfleet United F.C.">Ebbsfleet United</a>, but did not score again for just over a month until he scored a hat-trick in the away match against <a href="/wiki/Alfreton_Town_F.C." title="Alfreton Town F.C.">Alfreton Town</a> on 18 October.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> On 20 September, he was given a straight <a href="/wiki/Ejection_(sports)#Association_football" title="Ejection (sports)">red card</a> in a 5–2 home win over <a href="/wiki/Kidderminster_Harriers_F.C." title="Kidderminster Harriers F.C.">Kidderminster Harriers</a>, a match in which both teams played over an hour with ten men each.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Four days after his hat-trick, Vardy scored two more goals in a 4–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Bath_City_F.C." title="Bath City F.C.">Bath City</a>, a result which left Fleetwood two points behind leaders <a href="/wiki/Wrexham_A.F.C." title="Wrexham A.F.C.">Wrexham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the first round of the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> on 12 November, Vardy scored the second goal in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/EFL_League_One" title="EFL League One">League One</a> club <a href="/wiki/Wycombe_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wycombe Wanderers F.C.">Wycombe Wanderers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Fifteen days later, his goal in a 1–1 draw at Gateshead meant that he had recorded a goal in each of his last six appearances, totalling ten goals in that period;<sup id="cite_ref-base_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-base-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> he won the Conference Premier Player of the Month award for November.<sup id="cite_ref-Vardy_November_Honour_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vardy_November_Honour-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> On 13 December, Vardy confirmed a 2–0 win in added time as Fleetwood triumphed 2–0 away to <a href="/wiki/Yeovil_Town_F.C." title="Yeovil Town F.C.">Yeovil Town</a> in the Cup second round <a href="/wiki/Replay_(sports)" title="Replay (sports)">replay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 January 2012, Vardy scored twice in a 6–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Southport_F.C." title="Southport F.C.">Southport</a>, and six days later the team lost 5–1 at home to local rivals <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_F.C." title="Blackpool F.C.">Blackpool</a> in the third round of the Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> After the match, Blackpool manager <a href="/wiki/Ian_Holloway" title="Ian Holloway">Ian Holloway</a> made a £750,000 offer for him, which Fleetwood rejected, holding on for £1&#160;million and a <a href="/wiki/Loan_(sports)" title="Loan (sports)">loan</a> back to the club.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He totalled six goals in his first four matches of the calendar year.<sup id="cite_ref-base_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-base-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> On 21 February, he recorded a second hat-trick of the campaign, in a 6–2 win over Ebbsfleet United which left Fleetwood two points ahead of Wrexham at the top of the table.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Vardy scored both Fleetwood goals in a 2–2 draw against <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_City_F.C." title="Lincoln City F.C.">Lincoln City</a> on 13 April;<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Wrexham's draw against <a href="/wiki/Grimsby_Town_F.C." title="Grimsby Town F.C.">Grimsby Town</a> the next day gave Fleetwood the Conference title and a first-ever promotion to the Football League.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Vardy's 31 league goals saw him finish the season as the top scorer in the Conference Premier.<sup id="cite_ref-bsts_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bsts-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leicester_City">Leicester City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Leicester City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="2012.E2.80.9313_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–13_season">2012–13 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2012–13 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamie_Vardy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Jamie_Vardy.jpg/170px-Jamie_Vardy.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Jamie_Vardy.jpg/255px-Jamie_Vardy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Jamie_Vardy.jpg/340px-Jamie_Vardy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2098" data-file-height="3010" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamie_Vardy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vardy (left) warming up for <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> in 2013</div></div></div>
<p>On 17 May 2012, it was announced that Vardy would be signing for <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a> club <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> ahead of the 2012–13 season, for a reported fee of £1&#160;million, a <a href="/wiki/Non-League_football" title="Non-League football">non-League</a> record, which could potentially be worth up to £1.7&#160;million with add-ons.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The next day, he signed on a three-year contract until June 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On 14 August, Vardy made his debut for Leicester against <a href="/wiki/Torquay_United_F.C." title="Torquay United F.C.">Torquay United</a> in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a>, playing the entirety of the match at <a href="/wiki/Plainmoor" title="Plainmoor">Plainmoor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Header_(association_football)" title="Header (association football)">heading</a> the final goal in a 4–0 win.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Four days later he made his Football League debut at the <a href="/wiki/King_Power_Stadium" title="King Power Stadium">King Power Stadium</a>, a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_United_F.C." title="Peterborough United F.C.">Peterborough United</a> in which he set up a goal for <a href="/wiki/Andy_King_(footballer,_born_1988)" title="Andy King (footballer, born 1988)">Andy King</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first league goal in a 2–1 away defeat to <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> on 25 August. In September, he scored the winner in two 2–1 comeback victories, against <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-base_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-base-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Vardy's first season at the club was marred by his own loss of form, prompting criticism from some City supporters on social media, and he even considered leaving football until manager <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Pearson" title="Nigel Pearson">Nigel Pearson</a> and assistant manager <a href="/wiki/Craig_Shakespeare" title="Craig Shakespeare">Craig Shakespeare</a> convinced him to continue with the club.<sup id="cite_ref-Rise_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rise-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2013.E2.80.9314_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–14_season">2013–14 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2013–14 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The following season brought a turn around in Vardy's fortunes as he established himself as a prolific scorer in the Leicester attack as the club took a commanding lead at the top of the table.<sup id="cite_ref-Rise_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rise-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Vardy scored and won a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty kick</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C.%E2%80%93Leicester_City_F.C._rivalry" title="Derby County F.C.–Leicester City F.C. rivalry">local derby</a> as Leicester beat high flying <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C." title="Derby County F.C.">Derby County</a> 4–1 on 10 January 2014 and reaffirmed their position at the top of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Football_League_Championship" title="2013–14 Football League Championship">Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Vardy finished the season with 16 league goals as Leicester were promoted to the Premier League at the end of the season as champions,<sup id="cite_ref-lg1314_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lg1314-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and was named Leicester's Players' Player of the season at the club's awards.<sup id="cite_ref-lp1314_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lp1314-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2014.E2.80.9315_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–15_season">2014–15 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2014–15 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 19 August 2014, Vardy extended his contract until the summer of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-lg1314_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lg1314-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> After missing the first two matches of the season through injury, he made his <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> debut on 31 August 2014, as a second-half <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitute</a> in a 1–1 draw at home to <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>. On 21 September, Vardy delivered a <a href="/wiki/Player_of_the_match" title="Player of the match">man of the match</a> performance by scoring his first Premier League goal and setting up the other four as Leicester made a surprise comeback from 3–1 down to a 5–3 victory against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 April 2015, Vardy scored a 90th-minute winning goal in the Foxes' 3–2 victory at <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Impressive form throughout the rest of April, including another winning goal, against Burnley on 25 April, saw Vardy nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> award.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Vardy and Leicester ended the 2014–15 season in a safe 14th position having picked up 22 points since 4 April, capping things off by opening the scoring in a 5–1 victory against <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> on the final day of the Premier League season on 24 May.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2015.E2.80.9316_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–16_season">2015–16 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2015–16 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamie_Vardy_08_sierpnia_2015_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Jamie_Vardy_08_sierpnia_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Jamie_Vardy_08_sierpnia_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Jamie_Vardy_08_sierpnia_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Jamie_Vardy_08_sierpnia_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Jamie_Vardy_08_sierpnia_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Jamie_Vardy_08_sierpnia_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1137" data-file-height="1722" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamie_Vardy_08_sierpnia_2015_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vardy playing for Leicester City in 2015</div></div></div>
<p>Vardy started the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Leicester_City_F.C._season" title="2015–16 Leicester City F.C. season">2015–16</a> season by scoring the opening goal as Leicester picked up a 4–2 victory at home against <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> on 8 August 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> He scored the equaliser in Leicester's 3–2 comeback victory against Aston Villa on 13 September.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> With two goals in Leicester's 5–2 defeat to Arsenal on 26 September, Vardy reached seven league goals for the season, eclipsing his goal tally of the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 October, he scored the only goal of a home win over <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a>, the seventh consecutive Premier League match in which he scored, and his tenth goal of the league season.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Vardy scored in his eighth league match in a row on 31 October, and became only the third player ever to do so in the Premier League after <a href="/wiki/Ruud_van_Nistelrooy" title="Ruud van Nistelrooy">Ruud van Nistelrooy</a> (twice) and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Sturridge" title="Daniel Sturridge">Daniel Sturridge</a>, in a 3–2 win over West Bromwich Albion.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> A week later, he won and scored a penalty to secure a 2–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>, putting him on nine consecutive matches with a goal, behind Van Nistelrooy's Premier League record of ten.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Vardy also became the first player in the Premier League to score in nine consecutive matches in a single season, as Van Nistelrooy's 10 matches were at the end of the 2002–03 season and the beginning of the 2003–04 season.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> For his run of good form, Vardy was the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> for October 2015, the first Leicester player to be given the accolade since goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Tim_Flowers" title="Tim Flowers">Tim Flowers</a> in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 November, Vardy matched Van Nistelrooy's record of consecutive Premier League matches with a goal, opening a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> A week later, against Manchester United, he scored again to claim the record for himself.<sup id="cite_ref-plrecord_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plrecord-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> His run ended on 5 December when he did not score in a 3–0 win at <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>. Had he done so, he would have equalled the English top-flight record of 12 consecutive scoring matches set by <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Dunne" title="Jimmy Dunne">Jimmy Dunne</a> for <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> in <a href="/wiki/1931%E2%80%9332_Football_League" title="1931–32 Football League">1931–32</a>; the result nonetheless put Leicester on top of the table.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Following his goalscoring exploits, Vardy was again named as the Premier League Player of the Month for November,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> becoming only the fifth ever player to win the award in consecutive months.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> He was presented with a certificate from <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a> for his achievement.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamie_Vardy_and_family_after_victory_versus_Everton_at_the_King_Power_Stadium._(26831224691).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Jamie_Vardy_and_family_after_victory_versus_Everton_at_the_King_Power_Stadium._%2826831224691%29.jpg/300px-Jamie_Vardy_and_family_after_victory_versus_Everton_at_the_King_Power_Stadium._%2826831224691%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Jamie_Vardy_and_family_after_victory_versus_Everton_at_the_King_Power_Stadium._%2826831224691%29.jpg/450px-Jamie_Vardy_and_family_after_victory_versus_Everton_at_the_King_Power_Stadium._%2826831224691%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Jamie_Vardy_and_family_after_victory_versus_Everton_at_the_King_Power_Stadium._%2826831224691%29.jpg/600px-Jamie_Vardy_and_family_after_victory_versus_Everton_at_the_King_Power_Stadium._%2826831224691%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2975" data-file-height="2086" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamie_Vardy_and_family_after_victory_versus_Everton_at_the_King_Power_Stadium._(26831224691).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vardy celebrating Leicester's <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> title victory with his family in 2016</div></div></div>
<p>By January 2016, Vardy's transfer value had risen from £2.1&#160;million to £18.8&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-Leicester_City:_Why_we_are_all_rooting_for_the_Foxes_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leicester_City:_Why_we_are_all_rooting_for_the_Foxes-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> with manager <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Ranieri" title="Claudio Ranieri">Claudio Ranieri</a> describing him as "priceless".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> On 2 February, he scored both goals in a 2–0 win against Liverpool, the first being a long-distance <a href="/wiki/Volley_(association_football)" title="Volley (association football)">volley</a> described as "world class" by opposing manager <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klopp" title="Jürgen Klopp">Jürgen Klopp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Four days later, he signed a new contract to keep himself at Leicester until 2019, increasing his weekly salary to £80,000.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> On 10 April 2016, Vardy scored both goals (his 20th and 21st of the season) in Leicester's 2–0 win at Sunderland, becoming the first Leicester player since <a href="/wiki/Gary_Lineker" title="Gary Lineker">Gary Lineker</a> in the 1984–85 season to score 20 goals in the top division of English football. The result also secured qualification to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> for the first time in Leicester's history.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> A week later, Vardy scored the first goal of a 2–2 home draw against <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>, but was later sent off for <a href="/wiki/Simulation_(Association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Simulation (Association football)">diving</a> in the penalty area under pressure from <a href="/wiki/Angelo_Ogbonna" title="Angelo Ogbonna">Angelo Ogbonna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> He was charged with improper conduct for his reaction to the dismissal and was fined £10,000, as well as being suspended for two matches during a vital point of Leicester's eventually successful title campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With 24 league goals, Vardy was the second highest scorer in the Premier League for the 2015–16 season, alongside <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Ag%C3%BCero" title="Sergio Agüero">Sergio Agüero</a>, only one goal behind Golden Boot winner <a href="/wiki/Harry_Kane" title="Harry Kane">Harry Kane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Vardy was one of four Leicester players in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-PFA_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFA-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> he was later also named the <a href="/wiki/FWA_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="FWA Footballer of the Year">FWA Footballer of the Year</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FWA_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FWA-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and the 2016 Barclays <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Season" title="Premier League Player of the Season">Premier League Player of the Season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Barclays_Player_of_the_Season_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barclays_Player_of_the_Season-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2016.E2.80.9317_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–17_season">2016–17 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2016–17 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_0_Chelsea_3_(31510599933).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Leicester_0_Chelsea_3_%2831510599933%29.jpg/220px-Leicester_0_Chelsea_3_%2831510599933%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Leicester_0_Chelsea_3_%2831510599933%29.jpg/330px-Leicester_0_Chelsea_3_%2831510599933%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Leicester_0_Chelsea_3_%2831510599933%29.jpg/440px-Leicester_0_Chelsea_3_%2831510599933%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3622" data-file-height="3622" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_0_Chelsea_3_(31510599933).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vardy and <a href="/wiki/Wilfred_Ndidi" title="Wilfred Ndidi">Wilfred Ndidi</a> sandwich <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Victor_Moses" title="Victor Moses">Victor Moses</a> during Leicester's title defence.</div></div></div>
<p>On 3 June 2016, Arsenal made a bid of £22&#160;million for Vardy, triggering a release clause in his contract. Leicester offered him improved terms, and 20 days later he agreed to a new four-year deal, to be signed on his return from <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a>. Vardy rejected Arsenal's offer because Arsenal had not promised that he would be played in his normal position and because of the differences between the two club's tactics, with <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a> favouring possession and Leicester playing on the counter-attack.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 August 2016, he scored in a 2–1 defeat to Manchester United in the <a href="/wiki/2016_FA_Community_Shield" title="2016 FA Community Shield">2016 FA Community Shield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Twenty days later, Vardy scored his first league goal of the season in Leicester's first win of the campaign, beating Swansea City 2–1.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 December 2016, Vardy ended his ten-match drought within the opening five minutes against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>. He ended up scoring another two for his first professional <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> to help Leicester to a 4–2 victory, their first win in five league matches.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> A week later, he was sent off in the first half of a 2–2 draw at Stoke City for a challenge on <a href="/wiki/Mame_Biram_Diouf" title="Mame Biram Diouf">Mame Biram Diouf</a>; Leicester appealed unsuccessfully against his three-match suspension.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 February 2017, Vardy scored his first <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2016–17 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> goal in a 2–1 away defeat to <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla</a> in the first leg of the round of 16.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> On 18 April, he scored Leicester's equalizer in their second leg quarter-final match against <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a>, but nonetheless Leicester were eliminated 2–1 on aggregate.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h4><span id="2017.E2.80.9318_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–18_season">2017–18 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2017–18 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_1_Chelsea_2_(36325510703)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Leicester_1_Chelsea_2_%2836325510703%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Leicester_1_Chelsea_2_%2836325510703%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Leicester_1_Chelsea_2_%2836325510703%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Leicester_1_Chelsea_2_%2836325510703%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/da/Leicester_1_Chelsea_2_%2836325510703%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="328" data-file-height="466" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_1_Chelsea_2_(36325510703)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vardy playing for Leicester City in 2017</div></div></div>
<p>Vardy began his sixth season at the club by netting two goals in the 4–3 away loss to Arsenal in the opening day of <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Premier_League" title="2017–18 Premier League">the 2017–18 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> On 16 October, Vardy made his 200th appearance for the club in the 1–1 draw against <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Two weeks later, he scored the opener of a 2–0 home win against <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> in <a href="/wiki/Claude_Puel" title="Claude Puel">Claude Puel</a>'s debut match as Leicester manager.<sup id="cite_ref-Puel_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Puel-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 December 2017, Vardy netted his 50th Premier League goal in the 2–2 draw against Manchester United<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> and scored his 10th Premier League goal of the season on 20 January with a penalty kick in the 2–0 home win versus <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By netting a brace in the final day of the season, a 5–4 away defeat by <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>, Vardy reached 20-goal landmark in the Premier League for the second time in his career.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Overall, he made 42 appearances in all competitions, scoring 23 times as Leicester finished the Premier League in 9th place.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Vardy was the recipient of the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Goal_of_the_Season" title="BBC Goal of the Season">BBC Goal of the Season</a> award for a goal against West Bromwich Albion where he struck a first-time ball with his weaker foot that was looped over his shoulder at range by his strike partner Riyad Mahrez.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2018.E2.80.9319_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–19_season">2018–19 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2018–19 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chelsea_1_Leicester_1_(48574907327).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chelsea_1_Leicester_1_%2848574907327%29.jpg/220px-Chelsea_1_Leicester_1_%2848574907327%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chelsea_1_Leicester_1_%2848574907327%29.jpg/330px-Chelsea_1_Leicester_1_%2848574907327%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chelsea_1_Leicester_1_%2848574907327%29.jpg/440px-Chelsea_1_Leicester_1_%2848574907327%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4657" data-file-height="3726" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chelsea_1_Leicester_1_(48574907327).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vardy (left) playing for Leicester City in 2019</div></div></div>
<p>On 9 August 2018, just before the start of the 2018–19 season, Vardy signed a new four-year deal at Leicester, keeping him at the club until 2022, when he will be 35.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Vardy started the season as a substitute, scoring a 92nd minute consolation goal in the 2–1 away defeat to Manchester United on the opening match of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> He was sent off the following match after a harsh tackle on <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolves</a> defender <a href="/wiki/Matt_Doherty_(footballer,_born_1992)" title="Matt Doherty (footballer, born 1992)">Matt Doherty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sportbible_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sportbible-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> On 9 March 2019, Vardy scored his 100th goal for Leicester, scoring two goals in a 3–1 home win over Fulham.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> On 28 April 2019, Vardy scored another two goals, this time in a 3–0 home victory against Arsenal, bringing his goal tally in league football for Leicester to 100.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2019.E2.80.9320_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019–20_season">2019–20 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2019–20 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 25 October 2019, Vardy scored a hat-trick in a <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C._0%E2%80%939_Leicester_City_F.C." title="Southampton F.C. 0–9 Leicester City F.C.">9–0 away win</a> against <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 4 July 2020, Vardy scored his 100th and 101st goal in the Premier League in a 3–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> He became the first Leicester player to reach the 100 goal milestone and 29th overall in league history.<sup id="cite_ref-OneHundred_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OneHundred-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Of the 29 players to have scored 100 Premier League goals, only <a href="/wiki/Ian_Wright" title="Ian Wright">Ian Wright</a> (28 years 286 days) made his debut in the competition at an older age than Vardy (27 years 232 days).<sup id="cite_ref-OneHundred_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OneHundred-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With 23 goals, he won the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Premier League Golden Boot</a> for the first time in his career, followed by Southampton forward <a href="/wiki/Danny_Ings" title="Danny Ings">Danny Ings</a> and Arsenal forward <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Emerick_Aubameyang" title="Pierre-Emerick Aubameyang">Pierre-Emerick Aubameyang</a> both on 22 goals.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The 33-year-old Vardy became the oldest player to win the award, while <a href="/wiki/Didier_Drogba" title="Didier Drogba">Didier Drogba</a> was the previous oldest player to win the award at 32 when he led Chelsea to the Premier League title in <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Premier_League" title="2009–10 Premier League">2009–10</a> with 29 goals.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2020.E2.80.9321_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020–21_season">2020–21 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2020–21 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 26 August 2020, Vardy signed a new contract with Leicester City until 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> On 27 September 2020, he scored his second hat-trick against Manchester City in a 5–2 away win at <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Etihad Stadium">Etihad Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> On 25 October, he scored the only goal in a 1–0 win against Arsenal, to grant Leicester City their first away win at Arsenal since September 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> On 6 December 2020, while celebrating his last-minute goal in Leicester's 2–1 win against Sheffield United,
Vardy slid into and destroyed a corner flag which was carrying the <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_flag_(LGBT)" title="Rainbow flag (LGBT)">pride flag</a> colours as part of <a href="/wiki/Stonewall_(charity)" title="Stonewall (charity)">Stonewall's</a> Rainbow Laces campaign. Vardy later signed the flag and gifted it to Foxes Pride, Leicester's <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a>+ supporters group.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamie_Vardy_2018-06-28_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Jamie_Vardy_2018-06-28_1.jpg/170px-Jamie_Vardy_2018-06-28_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Jamie_Vardy_2018-06-28_1.jpg/255px-Jamie_Vardy_2018-06-28_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/83/Jamie_Vardy_2018-06-28_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="311" data-file-height="516" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamie_Vardy_2018-06-28_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vardy playing for <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>On 21 May 2015, Vardy was called up to the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">English national team</a> for the first time ahead of a friendly against the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a> and a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying">UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Slovenia_national_football_team" title="Slovenia national football team">Slovenia</a>. He made his debut on 7 June in the goalless draw against the Republic of Ireland at the <a href="/wiki/Aviva_Stadium" title="Aviva Stadium">Aviva Stadium</a> in Dublin, replacing <a href="/wiki/List_of_England_national_football_team_captains" title="List of England national football team captains">England captain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a>, for the final 15 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> On 30 August, Vardy was again called up to the England squad for the matches against <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_football_team" title="San Marino national football team">San Marino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a> in UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> being selected in the starting line-up as England ran out 6–0 winners against San Marino in <a href="/wiki/Serravalle_(San_Marino)" title="Serravalle (San Marino)">Serravalle</a> six days later.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Vardy scored his first international goal on 26 March 2016, equalising with a back heel from <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Clyne" title="Nathaniel Clyne">Nathaniel Clyne</a>'s cross, as a substitute in a 3–2 away win against <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Germany_2–3_England_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Germany_2–3_England-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> He scored again, three days later, the opening goal in a 2–1 defeat to the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Vardy made his tournament debut on 16 June, in England's second group match at UEFA Euro 2016, coming off the bench in the second half to score an equalising goal against <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales</a>, helping his team come from behind to win the match 2–1.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> During the tournament, there were media rumours of a feud between Vardy and fellow <a href="/wiki/Striker_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Striker (association football)">striker</a> Rooney, which were denied by manager <a href="/wiki/Roy_Hodgson" title="Roy Hodgson">Roy Hodgson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He was named in the 23-man England <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_squads#England" title="2018 FIFA World Cup squads">squad</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> He was used sparingly during the tournament, starting only the final group stage match against <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> as the England side reached the World Cup semi-finals for only the third time in their history.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 28 August 2018, Vardy stepped aside from the England national team, telling manager <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Southgate" title="Gareth Southgate">Gareth Southgate</a> that he did not want to be considered for selection unless there was an injury crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Player_profile">Player profile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Player profile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_wall_(30383776075).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Leicester_wall_%2830383776075%29.jpg/220px-Leicester_wall_%2830383776075%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Leicester_wall_%2830383776075%29.jpg/330px-Leicester_wall_%2830383776075%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Leicester_wall_%2830383776075%29.jpg/440px-Leicester_wall_%2830383776075%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leicester_wall_(30383776075).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vardy (wearing no. 9) in the Leicester City wall defending a free-kick, 2016</div></div></div>
<p>Vardy is considered one of the best strikers in world football due to his elite finishing ability, speed and positional awareness.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ian_Wright" title="Ian Wright">Ian Wright</a>, who also rose from non-League football to the Premier League and English national team, wrote in October 2015 that Vardy could be England's equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Salvatore_Schillaci" title="Salvatore Schillaci">Salvatore Schillaci</a> at UEFA Euro 2016: Schillaci, another late bloomer, began the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 FIFA World Cup</a> as a substitute behind more established players, and ended it as the top scorer.<sup id="cite_ref-wright_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wright-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Wright, who first learnt of Vardy when his former Burnley teammate <a href="/wiki/Micky_Mellon" title="Micky Mellon">Micky Mellon</a> signed him for Fleetwood, rates Vardy as a hard-working player with a good first touch, who creates constant work for defenders, and plays by instinct instead of being moulded by his managers.<sup id="cite_ref-wright_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wright-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Although Vardy usually plays in a central role as a striker, he is a versatile player, who is capable of playing in several attacking positions, and has also been used as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">winger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dai_dilettanti_all&#39;Inghilterra_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dai_dilettanti_all&#39;Inghilterra-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to his prolific goalscoring, Vardy is known for his high <a href="/wiki/Work_rate" title="Work rate">work rate</a>, relentless running, and direct approach, and is also capable of creating chances for his teammates.<sup id="cite_ref-Vardy_scales_new_heights_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vardy_scales_new_heights-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> He is considered an extremely fast and dynamic striker, with good positioning,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> and an excellent sense of space in the area;<sup id="cite_ref-real_deal_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-real_deal-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> he is also known for his ability to play on the last defender's shoulder, time his runs to beat the defensive line, and stretch opponents,<sup id="cite_ref-Vardy_scales_new_heights_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vardy_scales_new_heights-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> which, combined with his pace, makes him a threat on counter-attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-dai_dilettanti_all&#39;Inghilterra_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dai_dilettanti_all&#39;Inghilterra-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> A composed finisher and an accurate <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty</a> taker, he is also good in the air, and capable of striking the ball powerfully with either foot.<sup id="cite_ref-real_deal_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-real_deal-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Former England assistant manager and <a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a> pundit <a href="/wiki/Gary_Neville" title="Gary Neville">Gary Neville</a> commented on how Vardy's approach influences teammates: "He sets the tempo and the tone for the rest of the team and gives no other player behind him any excuse for not working hard."<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Lifestyle.2C_approach_to_training_and_late_development"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lifestyle,_approach_to_training_and_late_development">Lifestyle, approach to training and late development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Lifestyle, approach to training and late development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to Leicester vice-chairman <a href="/wiki/Aiyawatt_Srivaddhanaprabha" title="Aiyawatt Srivaddhanaprabha">Aiyawatt Srivaddhanaprabha</a>, Vardy drank heavily every night during his early days at the club, and would turn up at training still intoxicated. Srivaddhanaprabha discussed with Vardy over what he expected in his life, and Vardy gave up drinking and took training more seriously from then on.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other pundits, such as Jamie Jackson, have said Vardy refocused after the earlier night-club assault incident, and that the earlier arrival of Ella, his first daughter, was a stabilising force.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a>, Vardy spoke to the media about his unusual lifestyle choices for a professional sportsperson. He said that he does not exercise in a gym, and that he consumes <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull" title="Red Bull">Red Bull</a> caffeinated beverages and <a href="/wiki/Snus" title="Snus">snus</a> smokeless tobacco.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rebekah_Vardy_attends_England%E2%80%93Panama_match_at_the_2018_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rebekah_Vardy_attends_England%E2%80%93Panama_match_at_the_2018_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg/170px-Rebekah_Vardy_attends_England%E2%80%93Panama_match_at_the_2018_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rebekah_Vardy_attends_England%E2%80%93Panama_match_at_the_2018_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg/255px-Rebekah_Vardy_attends_England%E2%80%93Panama_match_at_the_2018_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rebekah_Vardy_attends_England%E2%80%93Panama_match_at_the_2018_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg/340px-Rebekah_Vardy_attends_England%E2%80%93Panama_match_at_the_2018_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg 2x" data-file-width="876" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rebekah_Vardy_attends_England%E2%80%93Panama_match_at_the_2018_FIFA_World_Cup.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vardy's wife Rebekah supporting him at the 2018 FIFA World Cup</div></div></div>
<p>Vardy is a lifelong fan of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a>, the club in his hometown.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before turning professional, Vardy combined playing non-League football with a job as a technician making medical <a href="/wiki/Splint_(medicine)" title="Splint (medicine)">splints</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, he received a conviction for assault following an incident outside a pub, and had to play with an electronic tag fitted for six months, while his curfew also limited his playing time at Stocksbridge Park Steels.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2015, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun on Sunday</a></i> published a video of Vardy at a casino the previous month, calling a man of East Asian origin a "<a href="/wiki/Jap" title="Jap">Jap</a>". He apologised for a "regrettable error of judgement" and was fined by Leicester, who put him on an educational course.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Vardy met <a href="/wiki/Rebekah_Vardy" title="Rebekah Vardy">Rebekah Nicholson</a> in 2014 while she was working as a nightclub promoter.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The couple married on 25 May 2016 at <a href="/wiki/Peckforton_Castle" title="Peckforton Castle">Peckforton Castle</a> in Cheshire, with <a href="/wiki/David_Nugent" title="David Nugent">David Nugent</a> as the best man.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Vardy has four biological children, three with his wife, and one from a previous relationship. He is also a stepfather to two children from his wife's previous relationships.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2015, Vardy launched <a href="/wiki/V9_Academy" title="V9 Academy">V9 Academy</a>, an annual week-long camp designed to offer coaching and guidance to 60 non-League players and offer them the opportunity to showcase their talent in front of scouts from league clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The same month, Stocksbridge Park Steels named their main stand after him.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> In December 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>-based food manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Walkers_(snack_foods)" title="Walkers (snack foods)">Walkers</a> brought out a limited edition 'Vardy Salted' <a href="/wiki/Potato_chip" title="Potato chip">crisp</a> flavour, in recognition of Vardy's goalscoring run.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Butchart" title="Adrian Butchart">Adrian Butchart</a>, English writer of the <a href="/wiki/Goal!_(film_series)" title="Goal! (film series)"><i>Goal!</i></a> series of football-related fiction films, finished a script in 2016 for a film about Vardy.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Vardy is an ambassador for Dorothy Goodman School, a special needs school in <a href="/wiki/Hinckley" title="Hinckley">Hinckley</a>, Leicestershire.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club">Club</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jamie_Vardy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Club">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
